GPT-4o on 7.NS.A.1-fraction

Common Core Standard 7.NS.A.1-fraction

This standard covers the following:

Apply and extend previous understandings of addition and subtraction to add and subtract rational numbers; represent addition and subtraction on a horizontal or vertical number line diagram.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Math problem: Determine the value of the sum when adding (74 / 63) and (91 / 78).

GPT-4o: 

To determine the value of the sum when adding \(\frac{74}{63}\) and \(\frac{91}{78}\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

1. The denominators are 63 and 78. We need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of these two numbers.
2. The prime factorization of 63 is \(63 = 3^2 \times 7\).
3. The prime factorization of 78 is \(78 = 2 \times 3 \times 13\).
4. The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
   - The highest power of 2 is \(2^1\).
   - The highest power of 3 is \(3^2\).
   - The highest power of 7 is \(7^1\).
   - The highest power of 13 is \(13^1\).

Thus, the LCM of 63 and 78 is \(2^1 \times 3^2 \times 7^1 \times 13^1 = 2 \times 9 \times 7 \times 13 = 1638\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1638:

\[
\frac{74}{63} = \frac{74 \times 26}{63 \times 26} = \frac{1924}{1638}
\]

\[
\frac{91}{78} = \frac{91 \times 21}{78 \times 21} = \frac{1911}{1638}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{1924}{1638} + \frac{1911}{1638} = \frac{1924 + 1911}{1638} = \frac{3835}{1638}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{3835}{1638}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 3835 and 1638. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(3835 \div 1638 = 2\) with a remainder of \(559\).
2. \(1638 \div 559 = 2\) with a remainder of \(520\).
3. \(559 \div 520 = 1\) with a remainder of \(39\).
4. \(520 \div 39 = 13\) with a remainder of \(13\).
5. \(39 \div 13 = 3\) with a remainder of \(0\).

The GCD is 13. Therefore, we simplify \(\frac{3835}{1638}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 13:

\[
\frac{3835 \div 13}{1638 \div 13} = \frac{295}{126}
\]

Thus, the value of the sum is \(\frac{295}{126}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{295}{126}\)

Expected answer: 295/126

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the sum of (74 / 63) and (91 / 78), compute what will be the sum if you add the result to itself.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of \(\frac{295}{126}\) and itself, we need to add \(\frac{295}{126}\) to \(\frac{295}{126}\):

\[
\frac{295}{126} + \frac{295}{126} = \frac{295 + 295}{126} = \frac{590}{126}
\]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{590}{126}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 590 and 126. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(590 \div 126 = 4\) with a remainder of \(86\).
2. \(126 \div 86 = 1\) with a remainder of \(40\).
3. \(86 \div 40 = 2\) with a remainder of \(6\).
4. \(40 \div 6 = 6\) with a remainder of \(4\).
5. \(6 \div 4 = 1\) with a remainder of \(2\).
6. \(4 \div 2 = 2\) with a remainder of \(0\).

The GCD is 2. Therefore, we simplify \(\frac{590}{126}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[
\frac{590 \div 2}{126 \div 2} = \frac{295}{63}
\]

Thus, the sum of \(\frac{295}{126}\) added to itself is \(\frac{295}{63}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{295}{63}\)

Expected answer: 295/63

Correct? Yes

Problem: In the previous problem you calculated the sum of (74 / 63) and (91 / 78). Now, assume instead of 74 in the first fraction, there were 35. What is the new sum when you add (35 / 63) and (91 / 78)?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the value of the sum when adding \(\frac{35}{63}\) and \(\frac{91}{78}\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

1. The denominators are 63 and 78. We need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of these two numbers.
2. The prime factorization of 63 is \(63 = 3^2 \times 7\).
3. The prime factorization of 78 is \(78 = 2 \times 3 \times 13\).
4. The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
   - The highest power of 2 is \(2^1\).
   - The highest power of 3 is \(3^2\).
   - The highest power of 7 is \(7^1\).
   - The highest power of 13 is \(13^1\).

Thus, the LCM of 63 and 78 is \(2^1 \times 3^2 \times 7^1 \times 13^1 = 2 \times 9 \times 7 \times 13 = 1638\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1638:

\[
\frac{35}{63} = \frac{35 \times 26}{63 \times 26} = \frac{910}{1638}
\]

\[
\frac{91}{78} = \frac{91 \times 21}{78 \times 21} = \frac{1911}{1638}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{910}{1638} + \frac{1911}{1638} = \frac{910 + 1911}{1638} = \frac{2821}{1638}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{2821}{1638}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2821 and 1638. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(2821 \div 1638 = 1\) with a remainder of \(1183\).
2. \(1638 \div 1183 = 1\) with a remainder of \(455\).
3. \(1183 \div 455 = 2\) with a remainder of \(273\).
4. \(455 \div 273 = 1\) with a remainder of \(182\).
5. \(273 \div 182 = 1\) with a remainder of \(91\).
6. \(182 \div 91 = 2\) with a remainder of \(0\).

The GCD is 91. Therefore, we simplify \(\frac{2821}{1638}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 91:

\[
\frac{2821 \div 91}{1638 \div 91} = \frac{31}{18}
\]

Thus, the value of the sum is \(\frac{31}{18}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{31}{18}\)

Expected answer: 31/18

Correct? Yes

Problem: What is the result of adding 94/5 to 1/25?

GPT-4o: 

To add the fractions \( \frac{94}{5} \) and \( \frac{1}{25} \), we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 5 and 25 is 25.

First, convert \( \frac{94}{5} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 25:
\[ \frac{94}{5} = \frac{94 \times 5}{5 \times 5} = \frac{470}{25} \]

Now, we can add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{470}{25} + \frac{1}{25} = \frac{470 + 1}{25} = \frac{471}{25} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{471}{25}\)

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the result of subtracting 48/20 from 49/8? Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem of subtracting \(\frac{48}{20}\) from \(\frac{49}{8}\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

1. Simplify \(\frac{48}{20}\):
   \[
   \frac{48}{20} = \frac{24}{10} = \frac{12}{5}
   \]

2. The fractions we need to subtract are now \(\frac{49}{8}\) and \(\frac{12}{5}\).

3. Find the least common denominator (LCD) for 8 and 5, which is 40.

4. Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 40:
   \[
   \frac{49}{8} = \frac{49 \times 5}{8 \times 5} = \frac{245}{40}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{12}{5} = \frac{12 \times 8}{5 \times 8} = \frac{96}{40}
   \]

5. Subtract the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{245}{40} - \frac{96}{40} = \frac{245 - 96}{40} = \frac{149}{40}
   \]

The result is \(\frac{149}{40}\), which is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{149}{40}\)

Expected answer: 149/40

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 22/49 and 72/35? Provide your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \( \frac{22}{49} \) and \( \frac{72}{35} \), we first need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 49 and 35. 

The least common multiple (LCM) of 49 and 35 can be found by determining their prime factorizations:
- 49 = \( 7^2 \)
- 35 = \( 5 \times 7 \)

The LCM is the highest power of each prime that appears in these factorizations:
- LCM = \( 5 \times 7^2 = 245 \)

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 245:
- For \( \frac{22}{49} \):
  \[
  \frac{22}{49} = \frac{22 \times 5}{49 \times 5} = \frac{110}{245}
  \]

- For \( \frac{72}{35} \):
  \[
  \frac{72}{35} = \frac{72 \times 7}{35 \times 7} = \frac{504}{245}
  \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{110}{245} + \frac{504}{245} = \frac{110 + 504}{245} = \frac{614}{245}
\]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \( \frac{614}{245} \) if possible. We check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 614 and 245. The prime factorizations are:
- 614 = \( 2 \times 307 \)
- 245 = \( 5 \times 7^2 \)

Since there are no common factors other than 1, the fraction \( \frac{614}{245} \) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{614}{245}\)

Expected answer: 614/245

Correct? Yes

The least common multiple (LCM) of 245 and 21 can be found by determining their prime factorizations:
- 245 = \( 5 \times 7^2 \)
- 21 = \( 3 \times 7 \)

The LCM is the highest power of each prime that appears in these factorizations:

Problem: Imagine you originally had 22/34 of a basket of ripe apples instead of 22/49, and you also have 72/35 of a basket of oranges. How much do you have in total, given these new amounts? Provide your answer in simplified form.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \( \frac{22}{34} \) and \( \frac{72}{35} \), we first need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 34 and 35.

The least common multiple (LCM) of 34 and 35 can be found by determining their prime factorizations:
- 34 = \( 2 \times 17 \)
- 35 = \( 5 \times 7 \)

The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors:
- LCM = \( 2 \times 17 \times 5 \times 7 = 1190 \)

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1190:
- For \( \frac{22}{34} \):
  \[
  \frac{22}{34} = \frac{22 \times 35}{34 \times 35} = \frac{770}{1190}
  \]

- For \( \frac{72}{35} \):
  \[
  \frac{72}{35} = \frac{72 \times 34}{35 \times 34} = \frac{2448}{1190}
  \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{770}{1190} + \frac{2448}{1190} = \frac{770 + 2448}{1190} = \frac{3218}{1190}
\]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \( \frac{3218}{1190} \) if possible. We check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 3218 and 1190. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
- 3218 Ã· 1190 = 2 remainder 838
- 1190 Ã· 838 = 1 remainder 352
- 838 Ã· 352 = 2 remainder 134
- 352 Ã· 134 = 2 remainder 84
- 134 Ã· 84 = 1 remainder 50
- 84 Ã· 50 = 1 remainder 34
- 50 Ã· 34 = 1 remainder 16
- 34 Ã· 16 = 2 remainder 2
- 16 Ã· 2 = 8 remainder 0

The GCD is 2. Therefore, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{3218 \div 2}{1190 \div 2} = \frac{1609}{595}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{1609}{595}\)

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the sum of 49/79 and 18/21.

GPT-4o: 

To calculate the sum of the fractions \(\frac{49}{79}\) and \(\frac{18}{21}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 79 and 21 will be our common denominator.

Since 79 is a prime number and does not share any common factors with 21, the LCM of 79 and 21 is simply \(79 \times 21\).

First, calculate \(79 \times 21\):
\[
79 \times 21 = 79 \times (20 + 1) = 79 \times 20 + 79 \times 1 = 1580 + 79 = 1659
\]

Now, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1659.

For \(\frac{49}{79}\):
\[
\frac{49}{79} = \frac{49 \times 21}{79 \times 21} = \frac{1029}{1659}
\]

For \(\frac{18}{21}\):
\[
\frac{18}{21} = \frac{18 \times 79}{21 \times 79} = \frac{1422}{1659}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{1029}{1659} + \frac{1422}{1659} = \frac{1029 + 1422}{1659} = \frac{2451}{1659}
\]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{2451}{1659}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2451 and 1659. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(2451 \div 1659 \approx 1\) remainder \(792\)
2. \(1659 \div 792 \approx 2\) remainder \(75\)
3. \(792 \div 75 \approx 10\) remainder \(42\)
4. \(75 \div 42 \approx 1\) remainder \(33\)
5. \(42 \div 33 \approx 1\) remainder \(9\)
6. \(33 \div 9 \approx 3\) remainder \(6\)
7. \(9 \div 6 \approx 1\) remainder \(3\)
8. \(6 \div 3 \approx 2\) remainder \(0\)

The GCD is 3. Therefore, we simplify \(\frac{2451}{1659}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 3:
\[
\frac{2451 \div 3}{1659 \div 3} = \frac{817}{553}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{817}{553}\)

Expected answer: 817/553

Correct? Yes

Problem: After getting the sum of 49/79 and 18/21 from the previous problem, let's denote this sum as n. Calculate the result of adding 71/97 to n.

GPT-4o: 

We previously found that the sum of \(\frac{49}{79}\) and \(\frac{18}{21}\) is \(\frac{817}{553}\). Let's denote this sum as \(n\). Now, we need to add \(\frac{71}{97}\) to \(n\).

First, we need to find a common denominator for \(\frac{817}{553}\) and \(\frac{71}{97}\). The least common multiple (LCM) of 553 and 97 will be our common denominator.

Since 553 and 97 are both prime numbers, we can find the LCM by multiplying them together:
\[
553 \times 97 = 53641
\]

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 53641.

For \(\frac{817}{553}\):
\[
\frac{817}{553} = \frac{817 \times 97}{553 \times 97} = \frac{79249}{53641}
\]

For \(\frac{71}{97}\):
\[
\frac{71}{97} = \frac{71 \times 553}{97 \times 553} = \frac{39263}{53641}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{79249}{53641} + \frac{39263}{53641} = \frac{79249 + 39263}{53641} = \frac{118512}{53641}
\]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{118512}{53641}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 118512 and 53641. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(118512 \div 53641 \approx 2\) remainder \(111230\)
2. \(53641 \div 111230 \approx 0\) remainder \(53641\)

Since the remainder is 0, the GCD is 1. Therefore, \(\frac{118512}{53641}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{118512}{53641}\)

Problem: What is the sum of 95/46 and 65/31?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{95}{46}\) and \(\frac{65}{31}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 46 and 31. The least common multiple (LCM) of 46 and 31 is 1426.

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1426:

1. For \(\frac{95}{46}\):
   \[
   \frac{95}{46} = \frac{95 \times 31}{46 \times 31} = \frac{2945}{1426}
   \]

2. For \(\frac{65}{31}\):
   \[
   \frac{65}{31} = \frac{65 \times 46}{31 \times 46} = \frac{2990}{1426}
   \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{2945}{1426} + \frac{2990}{1426} = \frac{2945 + 2990}{1426} = \frac{5935}{1426}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{5935}{1426}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 5935 and 1426. The GCD is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{5935}{1426}\)

Expected answer: 5935/1426

Correct? Yes

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of \(\frac{95}{46}\) and \(\frac{65}{31}\) together twice, we first need to determine the sum of these fractions once, and then double the result.

We already found that:
\[
\frac{95}{46} + \frac{65}{31} = \frac{5935}{1426}
\]

Now, we need to add this result to itself:
\[
\frac{5935}{1426} + \frac{5935}{1426} = \frac{5935 + 5935}{1426} = \frac{11870}{1426}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{11870}{1426}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 11870 and 1426. The GCD is 2.

So, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{11870 \div 2}{1426 \div 2} = \frac{5935}{713}

1. Convert \(\frac{25}{63}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 126:
\[

\]

Thus, the sum of \(\frac{25}{63}\) and \(\frac{74}{6}\) is \(\frac{802}{63}\).

\[
\frac{854}{70} - \frac{79}{70} = \frac{854 - 79}{70} = \frac{775}{70}
\]

We can simplify \(\frac{775}{70}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor (GCD), which is 5:
\[

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Find the sum of 21/75 and 44/47.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \( \frac{21}{75} \) and \( \frac{44}{47} \), we need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 75 and 47, which are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1). Therefore, the common denominator is their product: \( 75 \times 47 \).

First, calculate \( 75 \times 47 \):
\[ 75 \times 47 = 75 \times (50 - 3) = 75 \times 50 - 75 \times 3 = 3750 - 225 = 3525 \]

Next, convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{21}{75} = \frac{21 \times 47}{75 \times 47} = \frac{987}{3525} \]
\[ \frac{44}{47} = \frac{44 \times 75}{47 \times 75} = \frac{3300}{3525} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{987}{3525} + \frac{3300}{3525} = \frac{987 + 3300}{3525} = \frac{4287}{3525} \]

The fraction \( \frac{4287}{3525} \) can be simplified if there is a common factor. Let's check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4287 and 3525.

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 4287 \div 3525 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 762)} \]
\[ 3525 \div 762 \approx 4 \quad \text{(remainder 477)} \]
\[ 762 \div 477 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 285)} \]
\[ 477 \div 285 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 192)} \]
\[ 285 \div 192 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 93)} \]
\[ 192 \div 93 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 6)} \]
\[ 93 \div 6 \approx 15 \quad \text{(remainder 3)} \]
\[ 6 \div 3 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 0)} \]

The GCD is 3. Therefore, we can simplify \( \frac{4287}{3525} \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 3:
\[ \frac{4287 \div 3}{3525 \div 3} = \frac{1429}{1175} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{1429}{1175}\)

Expected answer: 1429/1175

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 95/57 and 28/80?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{95}{57}\) and \(\frac{28}{80}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 57 and 80 will be our common denominator.

1. **Find the LCM of 57 and 80:**
   - The prime factorization of 57 is \(3 \times 19\).
   - The prime factorization of 80 is \(2^4 \times 5\).

   The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
   - LCM = \(2^4 \times 3 \times 5 \times 19 = 16 \times 3 \times 5 \times 19\).

   Let's calculate this step-by-step:
   - \(16 \times 3 = 48\)
   - \(48 \times 5 = 240\)
   - \(240 \times 19 = 4560\)

   So, the LCM of 57 and 80 is 4560.

2. **Convert each fraction to have the common denominator 4560:**
   - For \(\frac{95}{57}\):
     \[
     \frac{95}{57} = \frac{95 \times 80}{57 \times 80} = \frac{7600}{4560}
     \]

   - For \(\frac{28}{80}\):
     \[
     \frac{28}{80} = \frac{28 \times 57}{80 \times 57} = \frac{1596}{4560}
     \]

3. **Add the fractions:**
   \[
   \frac{7600}{4560} + \frac{1596}{4560} = \frac{7600 + 1596}{4560} = \frac{9196}{4560}
   \]

4. **Simplify the fraction \(\frac{9196}{4560}\):**
   - Find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9196 and 4560. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
     - \(9196 \div 4560 \approx 2\) remainder 76
     - \(4560 \div 76 \approx 60\) remainder 0

     The GCD is 76.

   - Simplify by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 76:
     \[
     \frac{9196 \div 76}{4560 \div 76} = \frac{121}{60}
     \]

So, the sum of \(\frac{95}{57}\) and \(\frac{28}{80}\) is \(\frac{121}{60}\).

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{95}{21}\) and \(\frac{28}{80}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 21 and 80 will be our common denominator.

1. **Find the LCM of 21 and 80:**
   - The prime factorization of 21 is \(3 \times 7\).
   - The prime factorization of 80 is \(2^4 \times 5\).

   The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
   - LCM = \(2^4 \times 3 \times 5 \times 7 = 16 \times 3 \times 5 \times 7\).

   Let's calculate this step-by-step:
   - \(16 \times 3 = 48\)
   - \(48 \times 5 = 240\)
   - \(240 \times 7 = 1680\)

   So, the LCM of 21 and 80 is 1680.

2. **Convert each fraction to have the common denominator 1680:**

     \[

     \]

     \[
     \frac{28}{80} = \frac{28 \times 21}{80 \times 21} = \frac{588}{1680}
     \]

3. **Add the fractions:**
   \[
   \frac{7600}{1680} + \frac{588}{1680} = \frac{7600 + 588}{1680} = \frac{8188}{1680}
   \]

4. **Simplify the fraction \(\frac{8188}{1680}\):**
   - Find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 8188 and 1680. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
     - \(8188 \div 1680 \approx 4\) remainder 468
     - \(1680 \div 468 \approx 3\) remainder 276
     - \(468 \div 276 \approx 1\) remainder 192
     - \(276 \div 192 \approx 1\) remainder 84
     - \(192 \div 84 \approx 2\) remainder 24
     - \(84 \div 24 \approx 3\) remainder 12
     - \(24 \div 12 = 2\) remainder 0

     The GCD is 12.

   - Simplify by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 12:
     \[

   - Further simplify \(\frac{682}{140}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 2:
     \[
     \frac{682 \div 2}{140 \div 2} = \frac{341}{70}
     \]

So, the sum of \(\frac{95}{21}\) and \(\frac{28}{80}\) is \(\frac{341}{70}\).

Problem: Calculate the sum of 14/57 and 92/42.

GPT-4o: 

To calculate the sum of the fractions \(\frac{14}{57}\) and \(\frac{92}{42}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 57 and 42 will serve as the common denominator.

First, we find the prime factorizations of 57 and 42:
- 57 = 3 Ã— 19
- 42 = 2 Ã— 3 Ã— 7

The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors present in either number:
- LCM = 2 Ã— 3 Ã— 7 Ã— 19 = 798

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 798:
\[
\frac{14}{57} = \frac{14 \times 14}{57 \times 14} = \frac{196}{798}
\]
\[
\frac{92}{42} = \frac{92 \times 19}{42 \times 19} = \frac{1748}{798}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{196}{798} + \frac{1748}{798} = \frac{196 + 1748}{798} = \frac{1944}{798}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{1944}{798}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1944 and 798. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
1944 \div 798 \approx 2.436 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 348)}
\]
\[
1944 - 2 \times 798 = 348
\]
\[
798 \div 348 \approx 2.294 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 102)}
\]
\[
798 - 2 \times 348 = 102
\]
\[
348 \div 102 = 3 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 42)}
\]
\[
348 - 3 \times 102 = 42
\]
\[
102 \div 42 \approx 2.428 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 18)}
\]
\[
102 - 2 \times 42 = 18
\]
\[
42 \div 18 \approx 2.333 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 6)}
\]
\[
42 - 2 \times 18 = 6
\]
\[
18 \div 6 = 3 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 6. We simplify \(\frac{1944}{798}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 6:
\[
\frac{1944 \div 6}{798 \div 6} = \frac{324}{133}
\]

Thus, the sum of \(\frac{14}{57}\) and \(\frac{92}{42}\) is \(\frac{324}{133}\).

2. Convert \( \frac{65}{15} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 480:
   \[
   \frac{65}{15} = \frac{65 \times 32}{15 \times 32} = \frac{2080}{480}
   \]

\[
\frac{225}{480} + \frac{2080}{480} = \frac{225 + 2080}{480} = \frac{2305}{480}

Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[

\]

Thus, the sum of \( \frac{15}{32} \) and \( \frac{65}{15} \) is \( \frac{461}{96} \).

GPT-4o:

1. Simplify \(\frac{92}{29}\):

   - 41 divided by 33 equals 1 with a remainder of 8, so \(\frac{41}{33} = 1 + \frac{8}{33}\).

Now, we add the simplified fractions:
\[
\left(3 + \frac{5}{29}\right) + \left(1 + \frac{8}{33}\right) = 3 + 1 + \frac{5}{29} + \frac{8}{33} = 4 + \frac{5}{29} + \frac{8}{33}
\]

\[
\frac{5}{29} = \frac{5 \times 33}{29 \times 33} = \frac{165}{957}
\]
\[
\frac{8}{33} = \frac{8 \times 29}{33 \times 29} = \frac{232}{957}
\]

Now, add the fractions:
\[
\frac{165}{957} + \frac{232}{957} = \frac{165 + 232}{957} = \frac{397}{957}
\]

Thus, the expression becomes:
\[
4 + \frac{397}{957}
\]

Since \(\frac{397}{957}\) cannot be simplified further, the final answer is:
\[
4 + \frac{397}{957}
\]

- 57 = 3 Ã— 19
- 99 = 3Â² Ã— 11

- LCM = 3Â² Ã— 11 Ã— 19 = 9 Ã— 11 Ã— 19

- 9 Ã— 11 = 99
- 99 Ã— 19 = 1881

So, the LCM of 57 and 99 is 1881.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the sum of 58/30 and 49/37 and leave your answer as a fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To calculate the sum of the fractions \(\frac{58}{30}\) and \(\frac{49}{37}\), we need to find a common denominator. The common denominator for 30 and 37 is their product, 30 * 37 = 1110.

First, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator:

\[
\frac{58}{30} = \frac{58 \times 37}{30 \times 37} = \frac{2146}{1110}
\]

\[
\frac{49}{37} = \frac{49 \times 30}{37 \times 30} = \frac{1470}{1110}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{2146}{1110} + \frac{1470}{1110} = \frac{2146 + 1470}{1110} = \frac{3616}{1110}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{3616}{1110}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 3616 and 1110. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(3616 \div 1110 = 3\) remainder \(286\)
2. \(1110 \div 286 = 3\) remainder \(252\)
3. \(286 \div 252 = 1\) remainder \(34\)
4. \(252 \div 34 = 7\) remainder \(14\)
5. \(34 \div 14 = 2\) remainder \(6\)
6. \(14 \div 6 = 2\) remainder \(2\)
7. \(6 \div 2 = 3\) remainder \(0\)

The GCD is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[
\frac{3616 \div 2}{1110 \div 2} = \frac{1808}{555}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is \(\frac{1808}{555}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{1808}{555}\)

Expected answer: 1808/555

Correct? Yes

\[

\]

So, the final unsimplified fraction is:

\frac{9537}{7110}

   \[

\frac{47}{7} = \frac{47 \times 9}{7 \times 9} = \frac{423}{63}
\]
\[
\frac{5}{9} = \frac{5 \times 7}{9 \times 7} = \frac{35}{63}
\]

Now, subtract the fractions:
\[
\frac{423}{63} - \frac{35}{63} = \frac{423 - 35}{63} = \frac{388}{63}
\]

The fraction \(\frac{388}{63}\) is already in its simplest form because 388 and 63 have no common factors other than 1.

### Answer: \(\frac{388}{63}\)

Expected answer: 388/63

   - 79 is a prime number.
   - 38 can be factored into \( 2 \times 19 \).

Since 79 and 38 have no common factors other than 1, their LCM is simply \( 79 \times 38 \).

2. **Calculate the LCM:**
   \[
   79 \times 38 = 3002
   \]

   \]

Thus, the sum of \( \frac{60}{79} \) and \( \frac{53}{38} \) is \( \frac{6467}{3002} \).

Problem: Solve the following fraction equation: 39/48 + 19/84.

GPT-4o: 

To solve the fraction equation \( \frac{39}{48} + \frac{19}{84} \), we need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

First, we find the least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators 48 and 84.

The prime factorization of 48 is:
\[ 48 = 2^4 \times 3 \]

The prime factorization of 84 is:
\[ 84 = 2^2 \times 3 \times 7 \]

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
\[ \text{LCM} = 2^4 \times 3 \times 7 = 16 \times 3 \times 7 = 336 \]

So, the common denominator is 336.

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 336.

For \( \frac{39}{48} \):
\[ \frac{39}{48} = \frac{39 \times 7}{48 \times 7} = \frac{273}{336} \]

For \( \frac{19}{84} \):
\[ \frac{19}{84} = \frac{19 \times 4}{84 \times 4} = \frac{76}{336} \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{273}{336} + \frac{76}{336} = \frac{273 + 76}{336} = \frac{349}{336} \]

The fraction \( \frac{349}{336} \) is an improper fraction. We can convert it to a mixed number:
\[ \frac{349}{336} = 1 \frac{13}{336} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{349}{336}\) or \(1 \frac{13}{336}\)

   \]

   \[
   \frac{67}{15} = \frac{67 \times 10}{15 \times 10} = \frac{670}{150}

   \[

   \frac{670}{150} - \frac{81}{150} = \frac{670 - 81}{150} = \frac{589}{150}
   \]

Problem: Calculate the sum of 38/59 and 80/94.

GPT-4o: 

To calculate the sum of the fractions \(\frac{38}{59}\) and \(\frac{80}{94}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 59 and 94 will serve as the common denominator.

First, let's factorize the denominators:
- 59 is a prime number.
- 94 can be factored into \(2 \times 47\).

Since 59 and 47 are both prime and do not share any common factors, the LCM of 59 and 94 is simply \(59 \times 94\).

Now, let's convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[
\frac{38}{59} = \frac{38 \times 94}{59 \times 94} = \frac{3572}{5546}
\]
\[
\frac{80}{94} = \frac{80 \times 59}{94 \times 59} = \frac{4720}{5546}
\]

Now, we can add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{3572}{5546} + \frac{4720}{5546} = \frac{3572 + 4720}{5546} = \frac{8292}{5546}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{8292}{5546}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 8292 and 5546. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
8292 \div 5546 \approx 1.495 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
8292 - 5546 = 2746
\]
\[
5546 \div 2746 \approx 2.02 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
5546 - 2 \times 2746 = 54
\]
\[
2746 \div 54 \approx 50.85 \quad \text{(integer part is 50)}
\]
\[
2746 - 50 \times 54 = 46
\]
\[
54 \div 46 \approx 1.17 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
54 - 46 = 8
\]
\[
46 \div 8 \approx 5.75 \quad \text{(integer part is 5)}
\]
\[
46 - 5 \times 8 = 6
\]
\[
8 \div 6 \approx 1.33 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
8 - 6 = 2
\]
\[
6 \div 2 = 3
\]
\[
6 - 3 \times 2 = 0
\]

The GCD is 2. Therefore, we simplify \(\frac{8292}{5546}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{8292 \div 2}{5546 \div 2} = \frac{4146}{2773}

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 49/75 and 88/58?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{49}{75}\) and \(\frac{88}{58}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 75 and 58 will serve as the common denominator.

1. **Find the LCM of 75 and 58:**
   - The prime factorization of 75 is \(3 \times 5^2\).
   - The prime factorization of 58 is \(2 \times 29\).

   The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors involved:
   \[
   \text{LCM}(75, 58) = 2 \times 3 \times 5^2 \times 29 = 2 \times 3 \times 25 \times 29 = 4350
   \]

2. **Convert each fraction to have the common denominator 4350:**
   - For \(\frac{49}{75}\):
     \[
     \frac{49}{75} = \frac{49 \times 58}{75 \times 58} = \frac{2842}{4350}
     \]

   - For \(\frac{88}{58}\):
     \[
     \frac{88}{58} = \frac{88 \times 75}{58 \times 75} = \frac{6600}{4350}
     \]

3. **Add the fractions:**
   \[
   \frac{2842}{4350} + \frac{6600}{4350} = \frac{2842 + 6600}{4350} = \frac{9442}{4350}
   \]

4. **Simplify the resulting fraction:**
   - To simplify \(\frac{9442}{4350}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9442 and 4350.
   - Using the Euclidean algorithm:
     \[
     \text{GCD}(9442, 4350) = 2
     \]

   - Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
     \[
     \frac{9442 \div 2}{4350 \div 2} = \frac{4721}{2175}
     \]

Thus, the sum of \(\frac{49}{75}\) and \(\frac{88}{58}\) is \(\frac{4721}{2175}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{4721}{2175}\)

Expected answer: 4721/2175

Correct? Yes

To solve the expression \(\left(\frac{77}{30} + \frac{18}{51}\right)\), we need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

First, let's simplify \(\frac{18}{51}\):
- The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 18 and 51 is 3.
- So, \(\frac{18}{51} = \frac{18 \div 3}{51 \div 3} = \frac{6}{17}\).

Now, we have the expression \(\left(\frac{77}{30} + \frac{6}{17}\right)\).

Next, we find the least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators 30 and 17:
- Since 17 is a prime number and does not divide 30, the LCM of 30 and 17 is \(30 \times 17 = 510\).

Now, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 510:
- \(\frac{77}{30} = \frac{77 \times 17}{30 \times 17} = \frac{1309}{510}\).
- \(\frac{6}{17} = \frac{6 \times 30}{17 \times 30} = \frac{180}{510}\).

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[
\frac{1309}{510} + \frac{180}{510} = \frac{1309 + 180}{510} = \frac{1489}{510}.
\]

The fraction \(\frac{1489}{510}\) is already in its simplest form because 1489 and 510 have no common factors other than 1.

- Since 37 is a prime number and does not divide 30, the LCM of 30 and 37 is \(30 \times 37 = 1110\).

- \(\frac{77}{30} = \frac{77 \times 37}{30 \times 37} = \frac{2849}{1110}\).

The fraction \(\frac{3119}{1110}\) is already in its simplest form because 3119 and 1110 have no common factors other than 1.

- 84 = 2^2 * 3 * 7
- 34 = 2 * 17

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
- LCM = 2^2 * 3 * 7 * 17 = 4 * 3 * 7 * 17 = 1428

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 1428:
- For \(\frac{89}{84}\):
  \[
  \frac{89}{84} = \frac{89 \times 17}{84 \times 17} = \frac{1513}{1428}
  \]

- For \(\frac{75}{34}\):

  \]

\[

\]

The fraction \(\frac{4663}{1428}\) is already in its simplest form because 4663 and 1428 have no common factors other than 1.

\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{9326}{1428}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9326 and 1428 to simplify the fraction.

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
1. \(9326 \div 1428 \approx 6.53\) (integer part is 6)
2. \(9326 - 6 \times 1428 = 9326 - 8568 = 758\)
3. \(1428 \div 758 \approx 1.88\) (integer part is 1)

5. \(758 \div 670 \approx 1.13\) (integer part is 1)

8. \(670 - 7 \times 88 = 670 - 616 = 54\)
9. \(88 \div 54 \approx 1.63\) (integer part is 1)

16. \(20 - 1 \times 14 = 20 - 14 = 6\)
17. \(14 \div 6 \approx 2.33\) (integer part is 2)
18. \(14 - 2 \times 6 = 14 - 12 = 2\)
19. \(6 \div 2 = 3\) (integer part is 3)
20. \(6 - 3 \times 2 = 6 - 6 = 0\)

The GCD of 9326 and 1428 is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

GPT-4o: 

To add the fractions \(\frac{51}{74}\) and \(\frac{44}{83}\), we need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 74 and 83 will be our common denominator.

First, let's check if 74 and 83 have any common factors other than 1. Since 83 is a prime number, it does not share any factors with 74 other than 1. Therefore, the LCM of 74 and 83 is simply their product:

\[ 74 \times 83 = 6142 \]

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{51}{74} = \frac{51 \times 83}{74 \times 83} = \frac{4233}{6142} \]
\[ \frac{44}{83} = \frac{44 \times 74}{83 \times 74} = \frac{3256}{6142} \]

Now, we can add the fractions:

\[ \frac{4233}{6142} + \frac{3256}{6142} = \frac{4233 + 3256}{6142} = \frac{7489}{6142} \]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{7489}{6142}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7489 and 6142. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \( 7489 \div 6142 \approx 1 \) remainder \( 1347 \)
2. \( 6142 \div 1347 \approx 4 \) remainder \( 754 \)
3. \( 1347 \div 754 \approx 1 \) remainder \( 593 \)
4. \( 754 \div 593 \approx 1 \) remainder \( 161 \)
5. \( 593 \div 161 \approx 3 \) remainder \( 110 \)
6. \( 161 \div 110 \approx 1 \) remainder \( 51 \)
7. \( 110 \div 51 \approx 2 \) remainder \( 8 \)
8. \( 51 \div 8 \approx 6 \) remainder \( 3 \)
9. \( 8 \div 3 \approx 2 \) remainder \( 2 \)
10. \( 3 \div 2 \approx 1 \) remainder \( 1 \)
11. \( 2 \div 1 \approx 2 \) remainder \( 0 \)

The GCD is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{7489}{6142}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{7489}{6142}\)

Expected answer: 7489/6142

Correct? Yes

Now, add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{595}{203} + \frac{1363}{203} = \frac{595 + 1363}{203} = \frac{1958}{203}
\]

Simplify the fraction if possible. In this case, 1958 and 203 have no common factors other than 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{1958}{203}\)

Expected answer: 1958/203

Correct? Yes
